Khul' Compensation: Non-Valuable Items Yield Nothing
Ruling on khul' compensation with invalid items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khul' compensation with non-mutaqawwim items and explain the legal reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
In khul', compensation must be legally valuable property; wine and pig yield nothing.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from the Hanafi school on khul' (divorce by mutual consent with compensation). The text states that if the wife offers wine or pig as compensation, the husband receives nothing. We will explore the underlying principle regarding what constitutes valid consideration in khul'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Read the passage: 'And if he divorces her by khul' in exchange for wine or a pig: nothing is due to the husband.' The act is khul', and the ruling is that the husband gets nothing.
Khul' requires the wife's consent and some compensation from her.
2
Recognize the key term: mutaqawwim
The commentary explains the difference: entering marriage is valuable (mutaqawwim), so it requires valid compensation; exiting marriage is not valuable, so if the offered compensation is invalid, the husband loses his right.
Mutaqawwim means property that is legally owned and usable without prohibition.
3
Understand the reasoning
Dukhul al-bud' (entering the vulva) is mutaqawwim, so it can only be owned with a proper consideration. Khuruj (exiting) is not mutaqawwim, therefore it does not demand valid compensation. If the wife gives non-mutaqawwim items, the husband cannot claim them.
This reasoning distinguishes between the value of marital rights and the act of divorce.
4
Apply the rule
If the wife offers wine (which is not mutaqawwim), the husband receives nothing. The same applies to a pig or any other non-valuable item.
The ruling is not limited to wine and pig; any non-mutaqawwim item yields the same result.
5
Note the scope
This ruling applies specifically to khul'. In a regular talaq (unilateral divorce), the husband does not receive compensation, so this issue does not arise.
Khul' is distinct because it is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for consideration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن خالعها على خمرٍ أو خنزير: لا شيء للزوج.
والفرق أن دخول البضع متقوم، فلا يُملك إلا بعوض، وخروجه غيرُ متقوم
And if he divorces her by khul' in exchange for wine or a pig: nothing is due to the husband. The difference is that entering the vulva is valuable (mutaqawwim), so it cannot be owned except with compensation, while exiting it is not valuable.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation). If the wife offers wine or pig as compensation, the husband gets nothing because these items are not legally valid property in Islamic law. The commentator explains the underlying principle: entering into a marriage (dakhul al-bud') is considered valuable, so it requires proper compensation (mahr or khul' consideration). However, exiting the marriage (khuruj) is not considered valuable, hence it does not require valid compensation. Therefore, if the wife offers invalid items, the husband loses his right to compensation. This is a concise statement of the majority Hanafi position.

Key Terms
خالعها (khāla'ahā): He divorced her by khul', where the wife pays compensation to obtain divorce.
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Legally valuable property that can be owned and used without prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In khul', if the wife offers wine as compensation, what does the husband receive according to the Hanafi school?
A) The wine itself, since it is a valid commodity.
B) Nothing, because wine is not legally valuable property.
C) The value of the wine in dirhams.
D) A different compensatory gift of the same value.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi khul', the wife's compensation must be mutaqawwim; if she offers non-mutaqawwim items like wine or pig, the husband receives nothing.

The Linguistic and Legal Definition of Talāq and Its Three Categories
Linguistic and legal definitions of divorce with the threefold classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of talāq in Hanafi fiqh and classify any divorce scenario into one of the three categories: ahsan, sunna, or bid'a.

Core Idea
Talāq linguistically means release; legally it dissolves the marriage knot, but in Hanafi law, a rajʿī divorce does not end ownership until the idda expires.

Divorce (talāq) is one of the most significant acts in Islamic family law, carrying serious worldly and religious consequences. This lesson opens the Book of Divorce by establishing what talaq means – both in language and in the sacred law – and then sorts all divorces into three overarching categories. Understanding these definitions and categories is essential before studying the detailed rules.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic and legal meaning
Identify the two definitions: linguistic (removing a bond) and legal (dissolving the marriage knot). Note the alternative legal definition 'dropping the right over the vulva' which emphasizes the personal right.
2
Understand the Hanafi principle of suspended ownership
Grasp that talāq does not immediately remove the husband's ownership (milk al-nikāḥ) in a rajʿī divorce; ownership is suspended until the idda expires. For ba'in or pre-consummation divorce, ownership ends immediately.
This principle is unique to the Hanafi school.
3
Identify the three categories
Recognize the three types: ahsan (one divorce in a purity period without intercourse), sunna (one divorce in each of three purity periods), and bid'a (sinful but valid forms like three divorces at once or divorce during menstruation).
Bid'a is sinful but the divorce is effective.
4
Apply the categories to scenarios
Practice classifying hypothetical divorces: e.g., a man says 'you are divorced' once during menstruation → bid'a; a man says 'you are divorced' once during purity → ahsan/sunna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
الطلاق على ثلاثة أوجه : أحسن الطلاق، وطلاق السنة، وطلاق البدعة .
كتاب الطلاق
هو في اللغة: عبارة عن إزالة القيد، وهو مأخوذ: من الإطلاق. تقول العرب: أطلقتُ إبلي ،وأسيري وطلقت امرأتي، وهما سواء، وإنما فرقوا بين اللفظين ؛ لاختلاف المعنيين فجعلوه في المرأة: طلاقاً، وفي غيره: إطلاقاً.
كما فرقوا بين حصان وحصان فقالوا للمرأة: حَصَان، وللفرس: حصان، وهما سواء في اللفظ، مختلف في المعنى.
وهو في الشرع عبارة عن المعنى الموضوع لحل عُقدة النكاح. ويقال : عبارةٌ عن إسقاط الحقِّ عن البضع، ولهذا يجوز تعليقه بالشرط. فالطلاق عندهم لا يُزيل الملك، وإنما يحصل زوال الملك عقيبه إذا كان طلاقاً قبل الدخول أو بائناً، وإن كان رجعياً: وقف على انقضاء العدة، أي لم يزل الملك إلا بعد انقضائها.
* قال رحمه الله : (الطلاق على ثلاثة أوجه أحسن الطلاق، وطلاق السنة، وطلاق البدعة(۱).
(۱) هذه الأقسام الثلاثة ذكرت في نسخ القدوري، ولم تذكر في نسخ الجوهرة.
Book of Divorce. Divorce linguistically is an expression for removal of the bond, and it is derived from 'release'. The Arabs say: 'I released my camel and my prisoner' and 'I divorced my wife', both are the same; they only differentiated between the two expressions due to the difference in meaning; so they made it for women 'talaq' and for others 'itlaq'. Just as they differentiated between 'hisan' and 'hisan': they say for woman 'hasan' and for horse 'hisan' – both same in pronunciation, different in meaning. And legally it is an expression for the meaning established for dissolving the knot of marriage. And it is said: it is an expression for dropping the right over the vulva. And because of this, it is permissible to suspend it upon a condition. So divorce according to them does not remove ownership; rather, removal of ownership occurs after it if it is a divorce before consummation or a ba'in divorce; if it is raj'i, it is suspended upon completion of the 'idda, i.e. ownership is not removed except after its completion. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'Divorce is of three types: the best divorce, sunna divorce, and bid'a divorce.' (1) These three categories are mentioned in copies of al-Quduri and not mentioned in copies of al-Jawhara.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Divorce (Talāq) in al-Qudūrī's Mukhtaṣar. It begins with a linguistic definition: talāq is derived from itlāq meaning 'release' – the same root used for releasing a camel or a prisoner. The Arabs distinguished the word for women (talāq) from the general release (itlāq) to mark the specific legal context. The author then gives the legal definition: it is the dissolution of the marriage contract. Some jurists define it as 'dropping the right over the vulva' which emphasizes the sexual aspect. A key Hanafi principle is stated: talāq does not immediately remove the husband's ownership (milk al-nikāḥ); rather, ownership is removed after the divorce takes effect. If it is a ba'in divorce or before consummation, ownership ends immediately. If it is raj'i (revocable), ownership remains until the 'idda expires. This distinction has practical consequences: during the 'idda of a raj'i divorce, the husband can take back his wife without a new marriage contract. Then the author classifies divorce into three types: أحسن الطلاق (the best), طلاق السنة (sunnah divorce), and طلاق البدعة (innovation divorce). The best is to divorce once during a period of purity from menstruation without intercourse. Sunnah is to divorce three times in three separate purity periods. Bid'a is to divorce three times at once or during menstruation. The footnote indicates that al-Qudūrī included these three categories in his matn, but some copies of al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah omitted them; the commentator (Ibn al-Ḥammām) likely included them as part of his commentary on al-Qudūrī.

Key Terms
الطلاق (al-talāq): Linguistically: removing a bond. Legally: dissolving the marriage knot by specific words.
الإطلاق (al-itlāq): General release, used for non-marriage contexts like releasing a captive or animal.
حل عقدة النكاح (ḥall ʿuqdāt al-nikāḥ): Dissolving the knot of marriage, i.e., ending the marital contract.
إسقاط الحق عن البضع (isqāṭ al-ḥaqq ʿan al-buḍʿ): Dropping the right to sexual access, an alternative definition emphasizing the personal right.
طلاق السنة (talāq al-sunna): Divorce in accordance with prophetic practice: one divorce in a purity period without intercourse.
طلاق البدعة (talāq al-bidʿa): Divorce that contravenes prophetic practice, e.g., divorcing during menstruation or three divorces at once.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, when does a revocable (rajʿī) divorce completely end the husband's ownership (milk al-nikāḥ)?
A) Immediately upon pronouncing divorce.
B) After the completion of the ʿidda period.
C) Only after a court order.
D) Upon consummation of a new marriage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, talāq is the dissolution of the marriage knot by specific words, but ownership in a revocable divorce persists until the 'idda ends, and divorces are classified into best (ahsan), sunna, and bid'a.

Talaq — Divorce

Definition of Talaq and Its Three Types
Defines talaq and classifies its types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define talaq linguistically and legally, and distinguish between the three types: ahsan, sunnah, and bid'ah.

Core Idea
Talaq is the removal of marriage's knot; the best form is one divorce in a clean period without intercourse.

Divorce (talaq) is a serious matter in Islamic law, and knowing its proper forms is essential. This lesson establishes the foundational definitions and classifications according to the Hanafi school. The source passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayra presents the linguistic and legal meanings, then categorizes talaq into three types: the best (ahsan), sunnah, and innovation (bid'ah). Understanding these categories helps a Muslim choose the most commendable way if divorce becomes necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and legal definitions
Locate the definitions: linguistically, talaq means 'removing a restriction'; legally, it means 'undoing the knot of marriage' or 'relinquishing the right over the vulva'.
Note the distinction between talaq and itlaq (general release).
2
Understand the threefold classification
The matn states talaq is of three types: ahsan (best), sunnah (prophetic), and bid'ah (innovative). Focus on the description of each.
Ahsan is the most commendable; sunnah is allowed but less than ahsan; bid'ah is sinful but valid.
3
Analyze the conditions of ahsan al-talaq
The best divorce is one pronouncement in a period of purity (tuhr) without intercourse, followed by letting the iddah expire.
These conditions ensure minimal harm and maximum clarity.
4
Note alternative classifications
The passage mentions that al-Karkhi divides talaq into only two types (sunnah and bid'ah), merging ahsan into sunnah. Also, other possible interpretations are given.
This is a legitimate intra-madhhab difference in categorization, not in rulings.
5
Apply the classification to a scenario
Given a divorce scenario, determine whether it falls under ahsan, sunnah, or bid'ah based on timing, number, and intercourse.
For example, a divorce during menstruation is bid'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق

الطلاق على ثلاثة أوجه : أحسن الطلاق، وطلاق السنة، وطلاق البدعة .

هو في اللغة: عبارة عن إزالة القيد، وهو مأخوذ: من الإطلاق. تقول العرب: أطلقتُ إبلي ،وأسيري وطلقت امرأتي، وهما سواء، وإنما فرقوا بين اللفظين ؛ لاختلاف المعنيين فجعلوه في المرأة: طلاقاً، وفي غيره: إطلاقاً.

كما فرقوا بين حصان وحصان فقالوا للمرأة: حَصَان، وللفرس: حصان، وهما سواء في اللفظ، مختلف في المعنى.

وهو في الشرع عبارة عن المعنى الموضوع لحل عُقدة النكاح. ويقال : عبارةٌ عن إسقاط الحقِّ عن البضع، ولهذا يجوز تعليقه بالشرط. فالطلاق عندهم لا يُزيل الملك، وإنما يحصل زوال الملك عقيبه إذا كان طلاقاً قبل الدخول أو بائناً، وإن كان رجعياً: وقف على انقضاء العدة، أي لم يزل الملك إلا بعد انقضائها.

* قال رحمه الله : (الطلاق على ثلاثة أوجه أحسن الطلاق، وطلاق السنة، وطلاق البدعة(۱).

(۱) هذه الأقسام الثلاثة ذكرت في نسخ القدوري، ولم تذكر في نسخ الجوهرة.

فأحسن الطلاق أن يُطلق الرجل امرأته تطليقةً واحدةً في طُهْرٍ واحد لم يجامعها فيه، ويتركها حتى تنقضي عِدَّتُها .

يعني: أنه: حَسَنٌ، وأحسنُ، وبدعي.

وهذا اختيار صاحب «الهداية»(۱).

وفي «الكرخي : هو على ضربين طلاق سنة، وطلاق بدعة. أما تقسيم الشيخ على ثلاثة أوجه فيحتمل أنه أراد طلاق سنة، وطلاق بدعة، وطلاقاً خارجاً عنهما، وهو طلاق غير المدخول بها، وطلاق الصغيرة، والآيسة.

ويحتمل أيضاً : أنه أراد طلاق صريح وطلاق كناية، وطلاقاً في معنى الصريح، وليس بصريح ولا كناية.

وهو ثلاثة ألفاظ يقع بها الرجعي، ولا يقع بها إلا واحدةً، وهو قوله: اعتدي، واستبرئي رحمك، وأنتِ واحدة.

* قوله: (فأحسنُ الطلاق: أن يطلق امرأته تطليقةً واحدةً، في طُهْرٍ لم يجامعها فيه، ويتركها حتى تنقضي عدتها).

فإن قيل: قوله : أحسن: ينبغي أن يكون في الطلاق ما هو حَسَنٌ، وهذا أحسن منه. قيل: هو كذلك ؛ لأن الطلاق ثلاثاً، في ثلاثة أطهار، لا يجامعها فيه : .١( ٢٢٦/١)
Book of Divorce. Divorce is of three types: the best divorce, divorce of the Sunnah, and divorce of innovation. It is linguistically: an expression for removing a restriction, derived from 'release'. The Arabs say: 'I released my camel and my prisoner' and 'I divorced my wife', both are the same, but they differentiated between the two expressions due to difference in meaning, making it in the woman: talaq, and in other than her: itlaq. Similarly, they differentiated between 'hisn' and 'hisn' - they say for a woman: hisan, and for a horse: hisan, both are the same in pronunciation, different in meaning. In shari'ah, it is an expression for the meaning established for undoing the knot of marriage. And it is said: an expression for relinquishing the right over the vulva, and for this reason it is permissible to suspend it upon a condition. According to them, divorce does not remove ownership; rather the removal of ownership occurs after it if it is a divorce before consummation or an irrevocable divorce, and if it is a revocable divorce: it is suspended until the iddah expires, meaning ownership is not removed except after its expiry. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (Divorce is of three types: the best divorce, divorce of the Sunnah, and divorce of innovation.) (1) These three divisions are mentioned in copies of al-Quduri, and not mentioned in copies of al-Jawhara. The best divorce is that a man divorces his wife once in a single period of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, and he leaves her until her iddah expires. This means: it is 'good', 'best', and 'innovative'. This is the choice of the author of al-Hidayah. And in al-Karkhi: it is of two types: divorce of the Sunnah and divorce of innovation. As for the shaykh's division into three types, it is possible that he intended divorce of the Sunnah, divorce of innovation, and a divorce outside of both, which is the divorce of one not consummated, the divorce of a minor girl, and the post-menopausal woman. And it is also possible: that he intended explicit divorce, metaphorical divorce, and divorce in the sense of explicit, which is neither explicit nor metaphorical. And there are three words by which revocable divorce occurs, and only one occurs by them: his saying: 'Observe your iddah', 'Make your womb free', and 'You are one'. His saying: (Then the best divorce: that he divorces his wife once, in a period of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, and leaves her until her iddah expires). If it is said: the word 'best' (ahsan) implies that among divorce there is 'good' (hasan), and this is better than it. It is answered: it is so; because divorcing three times in three periods of purity without intercourse is... (reference: 1/226)
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on divorce (talaq) in the commentary al-Jawhara al-Nayra. It begins by defining talaq linguistically and legally, then classifies it into three types as stated in the matn of al-Quduri. The author explains that linguistically, talaq means releasing a restriction, and it is used specifically for women in shari'ah. The legal definition is 'undoing the knot of marriage' or 'relinquishing the right over the vulva'. He notes that talaq does not immediately remove ownership of the wife; this depends on the type: if it is before consummation or irrevocable, ownership ends immediately; if revocable, it ends only after the iddah. The three types are: (1) the best divorce (ahsan): one divorce in a period of purity without intercourse, letting the iddah expire; (2) sunnah divorce (talaq al-sunnah); (3) bid'ah divorce (talaq al-bid'ah). The commentator explains that 'ahsan' is the best because it fulfills the sunnah and avoids bid'ah. He also mentions alternative classifications from al-Karkhi and al-Hidayah, and raises the possibility that the three types could refer to explicit, metaphorical, and intermediate forms. The passage emphasizes that the best form is a single revocable divorce in a pure state.

Key Terms
الطلاق (al-talaq): Linguistically: removal of a restriction. Legally: undoing the knot of marriage or relinquishing the right over the vulva.
أحسن الطلاق (ahsan al-talaq): The best form of divorce: one single divorce in a period of purity without intercourse, after which the wife is left until her iddah completes.
طلاق السنة (talaq al-sunnah): Divorce that conforms to the prophetic practice, typically including one or two divorces in a period of purity without intercourse.
طلاق البدعة (talaq al-bid'ah): Innovative divorce, such as divorcing during menstruation or three divorces in one sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for the best divorce (ahsan al-talaq)?
A) The divorce must be pronounced three times
B) The wife must be in a state of menstruation
C) The divorce must be in a period of purity without intercourse
D) The divorce must be irrevocable (ba'in)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the best divorce is a single revocable pronouncement during a clean period, avoiding intercourse, and allowing the iddah to complete.

The Best Divorce (Ahsan) and Classifications of Talaq
Defining the best divorce and its classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ahsan, hasan, and bid'i divorce, state their conditions, and explain the Hanafi classification debate.

Core Idea
The best divorce is a single pronouncement in a state of purity – the simplest is the most sunnah.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains the three types of divorce according to Hanafi scholars. Understanding these categories is essential for implementing the Sunnah in divorce and for grasping how Hanafi jurists classify actions based on their conformity to prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Locate the three terms: ahsan (best), hasan (good), and bid'i (innovative). The text initially defines ahsan, then expands to hasan and bid'i.
The passage first gives the ruling for ahsan, then explains that divorce is of three types.
2
Define each category with its conditions
For ahsan: single divorce in a tuhr without intercourse, then leave her to complete iddah. For hasan: three divorces in three tuhrs without intercourse. For bid'i: divorce during menstruation or in a tuhr after intercourse.
The text explicitly defines ahsan and hasan; bid'i is mentioned as the opposite of sunnah.
3
Note the classification debate
The commentator notes that al-Hidayah divides into three, while al-Karkhi divides into two (sunnah and bid'i). Two reconciliations are offered: the third category might be divorce of non-consummated/minor/menopausal, or it may refer to explicit/implicit/third type.
This shows how Hanafi scholars differ on taxonomy despite agreeing on rulings.
4
Recognize the sunnah status
Both ahsan and hasan are considered sunnah; ahsan is merely better. The term 'hasan' for three divorces is sometimes called 'the inferior of sunnah divorce'.
This emphasizes that the ruling is about preference, not permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
فأحسن الطلاق أن يُطلق الرجل امرأته تطليقةً واحدةً في طُهْرٍ واحد لم يجامعها فيه، ويتركها حتى تنقضي عِدَّتُها.
يعني: أنه: حَسَنٌ، وأحسنُ، وبدعي.
وهذا اختيار صاحب «الهداية»(١).
وفي الكرخي: هو على ضربين: طلاق سنة، وطلاق بدعة. أما تقسيم الشيخ على ثلاثة أوجه فيحتمل أنه أراد طلاق سنة، وطلاق بدعة، وطلاقاً خارجاً عنهما، وهو طلاق غير المدخول بها، وطلاق الصغيرة، والآيسة.
6 ويحتمل أيضاً: أنه أراد طلاق صريح وطلاق كناية، وطلاقاً في معنى الصريح، وليس بصريح ولا كناية.
وهو ثلاثة ألفاظ يقع بها الرجعي، ولا يقع بها إلا واحدةً، وهو قوله: اعتدي، واستبرئي رحمك، وأنتِ واحدة.
* قوله: (فأحسنُ الطلاق: أن يطلق امرأته تطليقةً واحدةً، في طُهْرٍ لم يجامعها فيه، ويتركها حتى تنقضي عدتها).
فإن قيل: قوله : أحسن: ينبغي أن يكون في الطلاق ما هو حَسَنٌ، وهذا أحسن منه. قيل: هو كذلك؛ لأن الطلاق ثلاثاً، في ثلاثة أطهار، لا يجامعها فيه : حَسَنُ، وهو طلاقُ السُّنَّة، وهذا أحسن منه(۱)
قوله: (وطلاق السنة : أن يطلق المدخول بها ثلاثاً، في ثلاثة أطهار).
وهو أن يطلقها تطليقةً في طُهْرٍ لا جماع فيه، ثم إذا حاضت وطهرت : طلقها أخرى، ثم إذا حاضت وطهرت : طلَّقها أخرى، فقد وقع عليها ثلاث تطليقات، ومضى من عدتها حيضتان، فإذا حاضت أخرى : انقضت عدتها.
وإن كانت من ذوات الأشهر : طلقها واحدةً على ما ذكرنا، ثم إذا مضى شهر: طلقها أخرى، ثم إذا مضى شهر: طلقها أخرى، فقد وقع عليها ثلاث، ومضى من عدتها شهران، فإذا مضى شهر آخر: انقضت عدتها.
(۱) كل من الحسن، والأحسن: سنّي، وتسمية ما إذا طلقها ثلاثاً في ثلاثة أطهار لا جماع فيها: بأنه طلاق حسن، وأنه السنة : لا وجه له، والمناسب تسميته بـ: المفضول من طلاق السنة. فتح القدير ۳۲۷/۳، ۳۲۸، البحر الرائق ٢٥٦/٣.
Book of Divorce. The best divorce is that a man divorces his wife with a single divorce in one period of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, and he leaves her until her waiting period expires. Meaning: it is good, better, and innovative. This is the choice of the author of Al-Hidayah. In Al-Karkhi: it is of two types: sunnah divorce and innovated divorce. As for the shaykh's division into three aspects, it is possible that he meant sunnah divorce, innovated divorce, and divorce outside of them, which is divorce of the non-consummated, the minor, and the menopausal. It is also possible that he meant explicit divorce, implicit divorce, and divorce in the sense of explicit but not explicit or implicit. And there are three expressions by which revocable divorce occurs and only one occurs: his saying: 'Observe your waiting period', 'Ascertain your womb', and 'You are divorced once'. He said: (The best divorce: that he divorces his wife with one divorce in a period of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, and leaves her until her waiting period expires). If it is said: His saying 'best' implies that there is a divorce that is 'good' and this is better than it. It is said: So it is; because divorce three times in three periods of purity in which there is no intercourse is 'good', and it is sunnah divorce, and this is better than it. He said: (And sunnah divorce is that he divorces the consummated wife three times in three periods of purity). It is that he divorces her once in a purity with no intercourse, then when she menstruates and becomes pure he divorces her again, then when she menstruates and becomes pure he divorces her again; thus three divorces occur upon her, and two menstruations have passed from her waiting period, so when she menstruates again her waiting period ends. And if she is of the monthly cycles: he divorces her once as mentioned, then when a month passes he divorces her again, then when a month passes he divorces her again; thus three occur upon her, and two months have passed from her waiting period, so when another month passes her waiting period ends. (1) Both 'good' and 'better' are sunnah; and calling it when he divorces her three times in three periods of purity with no intercourse as 'good divorce' and that it is sunnah has no basis; the appropriate naming is 'the inferior of sunnah divorce'. Fath al-Qadir 3/327-328, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 3/256.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Quduri defining the best form of divorce (ahsan). The text first gives the ruling: the best divorce is a single revocable pronouncement in a state of purity (tuhr) during which no intercourse occurred, followed by leaving her to complete her waiting period (iddah). The commentator then explains that divorce is of three types: good (hasan), better (ahsan), and innovated (bid'i). This threefold division is attributed to the author of al-Hidayah. However, al-Karkhi divides it into only two: sunnah and bid'i. The commentator reconciles this by suggesting that the threefold division may refer to sunnah, bid'i, and a third category outside both—namely, divorce of a non-consummated wife, a minor, or a menopausal woman—or it may refer to explicit (sarih), implicit (kinayah), and a third category that is like explicit but not quite. The text also lists three expressions that effect a single revocable divorce: 'Observe your waiting period', 'Ascertain your womb', and 'You are divorced once'. The commentary then addresses an objection: the word 'ahsan' implies a comparative, so there must be a lesser good (hasan). The response clarifies that hasan is the sunnah divorce of three pronouncements across three tuhr periods without intercourse, while ahsan is better because it involves only one pronouncement. The passage then defines sunnah divorce properly: for a non-pregnant woman, it is three divorces over three tuhrs with no intercourse in each, but for a woman of monthly cycles (i.e., one whose iddah is by months), it is three divorces with a month between each. The commentator emphasizes that both hasan and ahsan are sunnah, though some scholars consider the term 'hasan' for three divorces inappropriate; rather, it is merely the less preferred form of sunnah divorce.

Key Terms
أحسن (ahsan): The best form of divorce: a single divorce in a tuhr without intercourse.
حسن (hasan): A good form of divorce: three divorces in three tuhr periods without intercourse.
بدعي (bid‘i): Innovated divorce, e.g., divorcing during menstruation or in a tuhr after intercourse.
طلاق السنة (talaq al-sunnah): Divorce in accordance with the Sunnah, encompassing both hasan and ahsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of 'ahsan al-talaq'?
A) Three divorces in three tuhr periods without intercourse.
B) A single divorce in a tuhr without intercourse, leaving her to complete her iddah.
C) Any divorce that is not bid‘i.
D) Divorce of a non-consummated wife.

Key Takeaway
The best divorce (ahsan) is a single pronouncement in a state of purity without intercourse; both ahsan and hasan are sunnah, but ahsan is superior.

Divorcing a Pregnant Woman: Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the number of divorces for a pregnant woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar on divorcing a pregnant woman and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
For a pregnant woman, the sunnah divorce is three with monthly intervals (Abu Hanifa) or just one (Muhammad) — the majority holds three.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known ikhtilaf regarding the proper sunnah divorce for a pregnant woman. This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah presents the views of the two leading pairs of Hanafi imams. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to appreciate how the same usul can lead to different rulings in subsidiary matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, note that the text states the view of 'the two' (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and then the opposing view of Muhammad and Zufar. State each position clearly: one allows three divorces with monthly intervals, the other only one.
The phrase 'عندهما' refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
2
Understand the rationale
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf analogize the pregnant woman to the woman whose iddah is by months, requiring three monthly intervals. Muhammad and Zufar focus on the fact that the pregnant woman's iddah ends with delivery, so one divorce suffices for sunnah.
The underlying principle is how to define 'sunnah divorce' for a woman with a non-menstrual iddah.
3
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the husband follows the majority view and gives three divorces with monthly intervals, the divorce is valid and sunnah. If he follows Muhammad and Zufar and gives only one, that is also valid but, according to the majority, not the full sunnah.
Both positions are considered valid and within the school, but the mufta bihi is the majority view.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: three divorces with a month between each.
This is recorded in the zahir al-riwayah and is the dominant practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانت حاملاً فكذا عندهما يطلقها ثلاثاً للسنة، ويفصل بين كل تطليقتين بشهر .وقال محمد وزفر : الحامل لا تُطلق للسنَّة إلا مرة.
And if she is pregnant, then similarly according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa) he divorces her three times for the sunnah, and separates between each two divorces by a month. And Muhammad and Zufar said: The pregnant woman is not divorced for the sunnah except once.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sunnah divorce of a pregnant woman. The text states that according to the two (meaning Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), a pregnant woman can be divorced three times for the sunnah, with a month interval between each divorce. This is analogous to the case of a woman whose iddah is by months. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar al-Kufi hold that a pregnant woman should only be given a single divorce for the sunnah. The reason for their view is that the pregnant woman's iddah ends with delivery, so a single divorce suffices to observe the sunnah. The dispute arises from differing interpretations of the optimal manner of divorce for a pregnant woman. In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, allowing three divorces with monthly intervals.

Key Terms
الحامل (al-hamil): A pregnant woman whose iddah ends with delivery.
الشهر (al-shahr): A lunar month used as an interval between divorces for the sunnah method.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) She must not be divorced at all.
C) She should be divorced only once.
D) The ruling is the same as for a non-pregnant woman.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a valid internal disagreement regarding the sunnah divorce of a pregnant woman, but the mufta bihi is three divorces with monthly intervals.

Sunnah Divorce: Method and Conditions
Defines and explains Sunnah divorce method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Talāq al-Sunnah, explain its method for three categories of women (menstruating, non-menstruating, pregnant), and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the pregnant woman.

Core Idea
Sunnah divorce requires three separate pronouncements in three tuhr periods — a single pronouncement does not complete the separation.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira defines the proper method of divorce according to the Sunnah. The Hanafi school distinguishes between Sunnah divorce and bid'ah (innovative) divorce. Understanding this method is crucial for a husband who wishes to divorce in a manner that avoids sin. The passage also introduces an important intra-Hanafi difference regarding the pregnant wife.

Guided Path
1
Define Talāq al-Sunnah
Use the matn's definition as a starting point: 'that he divorces the one who has been consummated with three [times] in three pure intervals.'
The definition applies only to a consummated wife (madkhul biha).
2
Explain the method for menstruating women
Walk through the three-step process: one divorce in a tuhr without intercourse, then after menstruation and purity, the second, then similarly the third.
Two periods of the waiting period (iddah) pass during the process.
3
Explain the method for non-menstruating women
For women who do not menstruate (young, menopausal, etc.), the intervals are months: one divorce per month for three months.
This is analogous to the tuhr method, substituting months for tuhrs.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute for the pregnant woman
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that she should be divorced three times with month intervals. Muhammad and Zufar hold that only one divorce is sunnah.
The later relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Muhammad and Zufar.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The later Hanafi fatwa prefers the view of Muhammad and Zufar for the pregnant woman to avoid unnecessary prolongation.
A husband who divorces a pregnant wife three times with intervals commits a valid but not sunnah divorce.

Source Text

Book of Divorce. And the Sunnah divorce: that he divorces the one who has been consummated with three [times] in three pure intervals. Good, and it is the Sunnah divorce, and this is better than it. (1) pure intervals. His statement: (And the Sunnah divorce: that he divorces the one who has been consummated with three [times] in three pure intervals). It is that he divorces her one divorce in a pure state without intercourse therein, then when she menstruates and becomes pure: he divorces her another, then when she menstruates and becomes pure: he divorces her another. So three divorces have occurred upon her, and two menstrual periods of her waiting period have passed, so when she menstruates another [time]: her waiting period ends. And if she is of those with months: he divorces her one as we mentioned, then when a month passes: he divorces her another, then when a month passes: he divorces her another. So three have occurred, and two months of her waiting period have passed, so when another month passes: her waiting period ends. And if she is pregnant, similarly according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) he divorces her three for Sunnah, and separates between each two divorces by a month. And Muhammad and Zufar said: the pregnant woman is not divorced for Sunnah except once.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage defines and explains Talāq al-Sunnah (Sunnah divorce). The matn states that Sunnah divorce is to divorce a consummated wife three times in three tuhr periods (intervals of purity between menses). The sharh elaborates: the husband pronounces one divorce in a tuhr during which no intercourse occurred, then waits until she menstruates and becomes pure again, then pronounces a second divorce, and similarly a third. This results in three divorces and two menstrual periods of the waiting period have passed; after a third menstruation, the waiting period ends. For women who do not menstruate (e.g., those with months, such as young girls or menopausal women), the intervals are months: one divorce per month. For a pregnant woman, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to 'them' (likely Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), she is also divorced three times with a month interval between each; but Muhammad and Zufar hold that she should only be divorced once in accordance with Sunnah. The footnote (1) references Fath al-Qadir and al-Bahr al-Raiq for further discussion. This is a parsing exercise where the commentator expands on the matn's concise definition.

Key Terms
طلاق السنة (Talāq al-Sunnah): The legally prescribed method of divorce according to the Sunnah, defined as three pronouncements in three separate tuhr periods (or months) without intercourse.
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between two menstrual cycles, during which intercourse is permissible.
المدخول بها (al-madkhul biha): The wife with whom the husband has had sexual intercourse.
ذوات الأشهر (dhawat al-ashhur): Women who do not menstruate (e.g., due to young age, menopause, or illness) and count their waiting period by months.

Key Takeaway
Sunnah divorce in the Hanafi school consists of three separate pronouncements in three distinct periods of purity (or months), with no intercourse in each period, and for pregnant women the relied-upon position is to issue only one.

Innovative Divorce: Prohibition and Validity
Defines bid'ah divorce, its ruling, and proof for prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bid'ah divorce, identify its definition, and explain the proof from hadith for its sinfulness.

Core Idea
Triple divorce in one utterance is valid but sinful—the Prophet called it disobedience.

In this lesson, we examine the concept of bid'ah (innovative) divorce. The Hanafi school holds that such a divorce is effective (the wife becomes separated) but the husband commits a sin. We will explore the definition, the rationale based on the original prohibition of divorce, and the Prophetic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Define bid'ah divorce
Locate the definition in the text: divorcing his wife three times in one utterance or three times in a single tuhr period.
The key phrase is 'بكلمة واحدة أو ثلاثاً في طهر واحد'.
2
State the ruling (valid but sinful)
Note that the divorce takes effect (waqa'a al-talaq) and she becomes separated (banat), but the husband is 'asiyan (disobedient). This is the Hanafi position.
The sin is due to violating the Sunnah method of divorce.
3
Understand the rationale: original prohibition
The commentator argues that the original ruling of divorce is prohibition (hazr) because it severs marriage, which has religious and worldly benefits. Divorce is only permitted out of necessity, and that necessity is met by the Sunnah method (one divorce per tuhr).
This explains why innovatory divorce is sinful—it goes beyond the permitted necessity.
4
Analyze the hadith proofs
Two hadiths are cited: (1) Ibn Umar's exchange with the Prophet where triple talaq is called disobedience and separation, and (2) the report of Ubadah about a thousand divorces where only three count and the rest are sinful. Both prove validity and sinfulness.
The hadith of Ibn Umar is in Sahih Muslim; it directly links triple talaq to ma'siya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطلاق البدعة : هو أن يطلقها ثلاثاً بكلمة واحدة أو ثلاثاً في طُهْرٍ واحد .
فإذا فَعَلَ ذلك : وَقَعَ الطلاق، وبانت امرأته منه، وكان عاصياً.
* قوله: (وطلاق البدعة : أن يُطلقها ثلاثاً بكلمة واحدة، أو ثلاثاً في
طهر واحد، فإذا فعل ذلك : وقع الطلاق، وبانت منه، وكان عاصياً).
لأن الأصل في الطلاق الحظرُ ؛ لما فيه من قطع النكاح الذي تعلقت
به المصالح الدينية والدنيوية.
فالدينية : حفظ النفس من الزنا، وحفظ المرأة أيضاً عنه، وفيه تكثير
للموحدين، وتحقيق مباهاة سيد المرسلين صلى الله عليه وسلم.

And the innovatory divorce: that he divorces her three with one word or three in one pure interval. So if he does that: the divorce occurs, and his wife becomes separated from him, and he is disobedient. * His statement: (And the innovatory divorce: that he divorces her three with one word, or three in one pure interval; so if he does that: the divorce occurs, and she becomes separated from him, and he is disobedient). Because the original ruling of divorce is prohibition; due to what it involves of cutting the marriage bond which is attached to religious and worldly interests. As for religious: preservation of the soul from zina, and preservation of the woman also from it, and in it is multiplication of monotheists, and realization of the boast of the master of messengers, peace be upon him. As for worldly: the mainstay of livelihood is based on it; because the woman works inside the house, and the man outside, so their affairs are organized. So when it is like that, it contains the meaning of prohibition, and it is only for the need to escape from the snare of marriage, and that is achieved by dispersing divorce over pure intervals. And he is disobedient only because the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he disapproved of Ibn Umar's divorce during menstruation, Ibn Umar said: What do you think, O Messenger of Allah, if I divorced her three? He said: Then you would have disobeyed your Lord, and she would have become separated from you. (Narrated by Muslim) and Ubadah ibn al-Samit said: Some of our fathers divorced his wife a thousand times, and that was mentioned to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and he said: She becomes separated by three in disobedience, and nine hundred...
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage defines Bid'ah divorce (innovative/heretical divorce) and states its ruling. The definition: divorcing a wife three times in one utterance (e.g., 'You are divorced three times') or three times in a single tuhr period. The ruling confirms that such a divorce is effective (the wife becomes separated), but the husband is sinful for committing an innovation. The commentator provides the rationale: the original ruling of divorce is prohibition (hazr) because it breaks the marriage bond, which has many religious and worldly benefits. Religiously, marriage protects from zina and increases the Muslim community; worldly, it organizes livelihood. Therefore, divorce is only permitted out of necessity, and that necessity is fulfilled by the Sunnah method of dispersing the pronouncements. The sinfulness of innovatory divorce is proven by two hadiths: (1) When Ibn Umar divorced his wife during her menses, the Prophet disapproved, and when asked about a triple divorce, the Prophet said it would be disobedience and separation. (2) Ubadah ibn al-Samit reported that a man divorced his wife a thousand times, and the Prophet ruled that only three count as a valid divorce and the rest increase sin. This passage is an expansion on the matn, providing proofs from hadith and legal reasoning.

Key Terms
طلاق البدعة (Talāq al-Bid‘ah): Divorce pronounced three times in one utterance or in a single tuhr period; it is valid but sinful.
الحظر (al-hazr): Prohibition; the principle that the original ruling of divorce is disallowed due to its harmful effects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The divorce does not occur
B) The divorce occurs and he is not sinful
C) The divorce occurs and he is sinful
D) The divorce does not occur and he is sinful

Key Takeaway
Bid'ah divorce (triple talaq in one utterance or one tuhr) is valid and results in irrevocable separation, but the husband commits a sin by violating the Prophetic guidance.

intermediate

Bid'ah Divorce: Definition, Ruling, and Evidence
Defines bid'ah divorce, states the dual ruling of occurrence and sinfulness, and provides proofs from sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define bid'ah divorce, state the Hanafi ruling that it is effective but sinful, and identify the prophetic proofs that establish this ruling.

Core Idea
Triple divorce in one sitting is effective but sinful—the act is prohibited, yet the legal consequence binds.

The category of bid'ah (innovative) divorce is defined as any divorce that violates the prophetic sunnah in timing or number. The Hanafi school holds that such a divorce is valid and causes irrevocable separation, but the husband commits a sin. This lesson examines the definition, the default ruling of prohibition underlying divorce, and the evidence from the sunnah that supports both the validity and the sinfulness of bid'ah divorce.

Guided Path
1
Define bid'ah divorce
Identify the two scenarios given: divorcing three times in one utterance, or three times in one menstrual purity period (tuhr).
Also note the extension: two divorces in one tuhr is also bid'ah.
2
State the ruling in two parts
Distinguish between the legal consequence (divorce occurs, woman becomes irrevocably separated) and the moral consequence (the husband is sinful).
The ruling is not that the divorce is invalid; it is valid but sinful.
3
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that the origin of divorce is prohibition (hazr) due to the harms of severing marriage, but it is permitted out of necessity. The sinfulness arises from violating the sunnah method of spacing divorces.
The hadith of Ibn Umar is the core proof.
4
Analyze the primary evidence
Examine the hadith of Ibn Umar: when the Prophet (saw) disapproved of divorcing during menstruation, Ibn Umar asked about divorcing three times, and the Prophet replied that it would be disobedience but effective.
Consider the two implications: 'Asayta Rabbak' (disobedience) and 'Baanat minka' (effectiveness).
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify the different narrations regarding a single irrevocable divorce (al-wahida al-ba'ina): in al-Asl it is against the sunnah, in al-Ziyadat it is not disliked if needed.
This shows that not all bid'ah forms are identical in weight.

Source Text

كتاب الطلاق

وطلاق البدعة : هو أن يطلقها ثلاثاً بكلمة واحدة أو ثلاثاً في طُهْرٍ واحد .

فإذا فَعَلَ ذلك : وَقَعَ الطلاق، وبانت امرأته منه، وكان عاصياً.

* قوله: (وطلاق البدعة : أن يُطلقها ثلاثاً بكلمة واحدة، أو ثلاثاً في طهر واحد، فإذا فعل ذلك : وقع الطلاق، وبانت منه، وكان عاصياً). لأن الأصل في الطلاق الحظرُ ؛ لما فيه من قطع النكاح الذي تعلقت به المصالح الدينية والدنيوية.

فالدينية : حفظ النفس من الزنا، وحفظ المرأة أيضاً عنه، وفيه تكثير للموحدين، وتحقيق مباهاة سيد المرسلين صلى الله عليه وسلم. وأما الدنيوية فقوامُ أمر المعيشة؛ لأن المرأة تعمل داخل البيت، والرجل خارجه، فينتظم أمرهما.

فإذا كان كذلك كان فيه معنى الحظر، وإنما للحاجة إلى الخلاص من حبالة النكاح ، وذلك يحصل بتفريق الطلاق على الأطهار. وإنما كان عاصياً ؛ لأن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام لما أنكر على ابن عمر الطلاق في الحيض، قال ابن عمر أرأيت يا رسول الله ! لو طلقتها ثلاثاً؟ قال : إذاً عصيت ربَّك، وبانت منك»(۱).

وقال عبادة بن الصامت طلق بعض آبائنا امرأته ألفاً، فذكر ذلك للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال: بانت بثلاث في معصية، وتسعمائة وأربعة وتسعون فيما لا يملك» (۱).

وكان عمر رضي الله عنه لا يُؤتى برجل طلق ثلاثاً إلا أوجعه ضرباً (۲)

وكذا إيقاع الثنتين في الطهر الواحد بدعة.

وكذا الطلاق في حالة الحيض مكروه؛ لما فيه من تطويل العدة على المرأة.

- وكذا في النفاس أيضاً.

واختلفت الرواية في الواحدة البائنة :

قال في «الأصل»: إنه أخطأ السنة ؛ لأنه لا حاجة إلى إثبات صفة زائدة في الخلاص، وهي البينونة.

وفي الزيادات»: لا يكره ؛ للحاجة إلى الخلاص الناجز.
Book of Divorce. And Bid'ah divorce: It is that he divorces her three times with one word or three times in one period of purity. So if he does that, the divorce occurs, and his wife becomes irrevocably separated from him, and he is sinful. His statement: (And Bid'ah divorce: that he divorces her three times with one word, or three times in one purity period, so if he does that, divorce occurs, she becomes separated from him, and he is sinful). Because the origin concerning divorce is prohibition; due to what it entails of cutting off marriage, which is connected to religious and worldly interests. As for the religious: preservation of the soul from adultery, and preservation of the woman from it as well, and therein is multiplication of monotheists, and realization of the boast of the Master of Messengers, may God bless him and grant him peace. As for the worldly: the sustenance of livelihood; because the woman works inside the house and the man outside, so their affairs are organized. So if that is the case, it contains the meaning of prohibition, but it is permissible due to the need for release from the marriage bond, and that is achieved by spacing divorces over purity periods. And he is sinful because when the Prophet, peace be upon him, disapproved of Ibn Umar's divorce during menstruation, Ibn Umar said: 'Do you see, O Messenger of God, if I divorced her three times?' He said: 'Then you would have disobeyed your Lord, and she would be irrevocably separated from you.' (Reported by Muslim). And Ubadah ibn al-Samit said: 'One of our fathers divorced his wife a thousand times, and that was mentioned to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and he said: "She is irrevocably separated with three in disobedience, and nine hundred and ninety-four in what he does not own."' (Reported by al-Daraqutni, said to be weak). And Umar ibn al-Khattab, may God be pleased with him, would not have a man brought to him who divorced three times without inflicting pain on him by beating. Likewise, effecting two divorces in one purity period is Bid'ah. Likewise, divorce during menstruation is disliked because it prolongs the waiting period for the woman. And likewise during postnatal bleeding. And the narration differs regarding the one-time irrevocable divorce: In al-Asl it is said that it misses the Sunnah because there is no need to establish an additional attribute for release, namely irrevocability. And in al-Ziyadat: it is not disliked due to the need for immediate release.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, addresses the category of Bid'ah (innovative) divorce. The commentator begins by defining it: divorce that violates the prophetic Sunnah either in number or time. The primary scenario is divorcing one's wife three times in a single utterance (e.g., 'You are divorced thrice') or three separate utterances in one menstrual purity period (tuhr). The ruling is that such a divorce is effective (waqa'a al-talaq) and causes an irrevocable separation (bainuna), but the husband commits a sin (asiyan). The commentator then explains the rationale: the default ruling of divorce is prohibition (hazr) due to the harms of severing marriage, which serves religious and worldly interests. Religiously, it prevents adultery and multiplies the community of monotheists; worldly, it maintains household order. However, divorce is permitted out of necessity for release from an unhappy marriage. The sinfulness is proven by the hadith of Ibn Umar: when the Prophet disapproved of divorcing during menstruation, Ibn Umar asked about divorcing three times, and the Prophet replied that it would be disobedience and effective. The commentator also cites the report of Ubadah ibn al-Samit and the practice of Umar (beating men who gave triple divorce). Then additional bid'ah forms are mentioned: two divorces in one tuhr, and divorce during menstruation or postnatal bleeding (disliked due to prolonging idda). Finally, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about a single irrevocable divorce (al-wahida al-ba'ina): according to al-Asl (by Imam Muhammad), it is also against the sunnah because the added attribute of irrevocability is unnecessary, but according to al-Ziyadat, it is not disliked if needed for immediate release.

Key Terms
طلاق البدعة (talāq al-bidʿa): Divorce that violates the sunnah in timing or number, such as three divorces in one utterance or one tuhr, or divorce during menstruation.
الواحدة البائنة (al-wāḥida al-bāʾina): A single irrevocable divorce that makes the wife immediately separated (bainuna sughra), without possibility of revocability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is invalid and no divorce occurs.
B) It is valid but sinful; three irrevocable divorces occur.
C) It is valid only if witnessed by two witnesses.
D) It counts as one revocable divorce.

Key Takeaway
Triple divorce in one sitting is a bid'ah that is effective (three irrevocable divorces) but sinful; the husband must repent.

The Two Aspects of Sunnah Divorce: Time and Number
Defines sunnah divorce into two aspects and specifies the scope of number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two aspects of sunnah divorce (time and number) and identify that the sunnah in number applies to both consummated and unconsummated marriages.

Core Idea
Sunnah divorce has two aspects: time and number; the number aspect requires one divorce per purity period for all wives.

Divorce in Islam is not simply a matter of uttering words; the Prophet ﷺ taught a specific practice (sunnah) that respects both the wife's waiting period and the possibility of reconciliation. This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira defines the sunnah divorce into two key dimensions: when to divorce (time) and how many pronouncements to give (number). Importantly, the ruling on the number applies to both consummated and unconsummated marriages, clarifying a common misconception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects of sunnah divorce
The text states 'sunnah in time' and 'sunnah in number'. Recognize that time concerns the appropriate period for pronouncing divorce (e.g., during a purity period without intercourse), while number concerns how many divorces to give (one per tuhr).
These two aspects are independent but both must be considered for a divorce to be sunnah.
2
Determine the scope of sunnah in number
The text explicitly says the sunnah in number 'applies equally to the consummated marriage and the unconsummated marriage'. This means even if the marriage was not consummated, the recommended practice is one divorce per unit of purity, not multiple pronouncements.
Some mistakenly think that since an unconsummated wife's divorce is irrevocable, the number restriction does not apply. The text rejects this.
3
Evaluate the footnote about the weak hadith
The commentary notes the supporting hadith (from Daraqutni) is weak (da'if). However, the ruling is based on strong principles and other evidence, so the weakness of this particular hadith does not undermine the fiqh position.
In Hanafi usul, a ruling may be supported by multiple evidences; a weak hadith can be corroborated by other proofs.

* قوله: (والسنة في الطلاق من وجهين: سُنَّةٌ في الوقت، وسنةٌ في العدد . فالسُّنَّةُ في العدد، يستوي فيها المدخول بها، وغير المدخول بها . ضعف.

(۱) سنن الدارقطني (٣٩٤٣)، وعزاه في مجمع الزوائد ٣٣٨/٤ للطبراني، وفيه ضعف.
He said: (And the Sunnah in divorce is of two aspects: Sunnah in time, and Sunnah in number. The Sunnah in number applies equally to the consummated marriage and the unconsummated marriage). Weak.

Commentary
This short passage identifies the two dimensions of sunnah (prophetic practice) in divorce. The first is sunnah in time, which relates to when the divorce is pronounced (e.g., during a purity period without intercourse for a consummated marriage, or any time for an unconsummated one). The second is sunnah in number, meaning that the husband should give one revocable divorce per purity period. The text notes that the sunnah in number applies to both women who have been consummated with (al-madkhul biha) and those not (ghair al-madkhul biha), indicating that for an unconsummated wife, the sunnah also recommends one divorce rather than three, even though her divorce is irrevocable. The phrase 'da'if' (weak) at the end likely refers to a hadith that was cited in the original source supporting this ruling; the commentator includes a footnote referencing the source (Daraqutni) and its weakness, which suggests that the ruling is based on strong principles even if the particular hadith is weak.

Key Terms
السنة في العدد (al-sunna fī al-ʿadad): The prophetic practice regarding the number of divorces, i.e., divorcing once per purity period rather than multiple times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Sunnah and Bid'ah in Divorce: Number and Time
Explains sunnah and bid'ah classifications of talaq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two dimensions of sunnah divorce (number and time), identify the conditions for each, and distinguish sunnah from bid'ah divorce.

Core Idea
The sunnah divorce is one pronouncement in a non-menstrual period without intercourse — avoid regret.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayirah explains the sunnah and bid'ah classifications of divorce. The author distinguishes between sunnah in number (one pronouncement for all wives) and sunnah in time (for consummated wives only: purity without intercourse). Understanding these categories helps avoid prohibited (bid'ah) divorce and ensures the husband follows the Prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dimensions
Recognize that sunnah divorce has two aspects: number and time. The passage explicitly states this bipartite division.
2
Analyze sunnah in number
Note that sunnah in number is one pronouncement, applicable equally to consummated and non-consummated wives. The term 'one' is called 'number' metaphorically.
The passage also discusses the effect of saying 'three with intention of sunnah' — only one falls immediately.
3
Analyze sunnah in time
Sunnah in time applies only to consummated wives: divorce must be pronounced in a state of purity (tuhr) where no intercourse has occurred in that cycle. For a pregnant wife whose pregnancy is apparent, this condition is also met.
Divorce during menstruation or postpartum is bid'ah because it lengthens the iddah.
4
Examine the evidence
The evidence includes the practice of Umar (painful punishment for triple talaq) and rational reasoning: triple talaq is prohibited out of fear of regret, and divorce during menses is disliked due to extended waiting period.
The argument is based on maqasid (preventing harm and regret).
5
Review the intra-Hanafi dispute
The passage notes a difference of narration regarding the single irrevocable divorce (al-wahidah al-ba'inah). Al-Asl considers it against sunnah; al-Ziyadat considers it not disliked due to necessity. Additionally, Abu Yusuf differs on the timing of subsequent divorces after remarriage.
The later preferred view (mufta bihi) follows al-Ziyadat and the general view on timing.

كتاب الطلاق

والسنة في الطلاق من وجهين: سنة في الوقت، وسنة في العدد. فالسنة في العدد، يستوي فيها المدخول بها، وغير المدخول بها.

وكان عمر رضي الله عنه لا يؤتى برجل طلق ثلاثا إلا أوجعه ضربا.

وكذا إيقاع الثنتين في الطهر الواحد بدعة.

وكذا الطلاق في حالة الحيض مكروه؛ لما فيه من تطويل العدة على المرأة.

وكذا في النفاس أيضا.

واختلفت الرواية في الواحدة البائنة:

قال في «الأصل»: إنه أخطأ السنة؛ لأنه لا حاجة إلى إثبات صفة زائدة في الخلاص، وهي البينونة.

وفي «الزيادات»: لا يكره؛ للحاجة إلى الخلاص الناجز.

* قوله: (والسنة في الطلاق من وجهين: سنة في الوقت، وسنة في العدد، فالسنة في العدد: يستوي فيها المدخول بها وغير المدخول بها).

والسنة في الوقت، تثبت في حق المدخول بها خاصة، وهو: أن يطلقها واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه.

لأن الطلاق الثلاث في كلمة إنما منع منه؛ خوفا من الندم، أن يبدو له، فيستدرك العقد عليها ثانيا، وهذا المعنى موجود في غير المدخول بها.

- ويقال: إن السنة في العدد: هو أحسن الطلاق، وهو أن يطلقها واحدة، لا غير.

- وسميت الواحدة عددا: مجازا؛ لأنه أصل العدد. فإن كانت غير مدخولة، فقد وجدت السنة في طلاقها من غير التفات إلى أمر آخر. وإن كانت مدخولة: فلا بد من النظر إلى الوقت، فإن كان يصلح للإيقاع: كان سنيا، وإن لم يصلح: كان بدعيا.

وقوله: يستوي فيها المدخولة وغيرها حتى لو قال قبل الدخول: أنت طالق ثلاثا للسنة: يقع واحدة ساعة تكلم، فإن تزوجها: وقعت أخرى ساعة تزوجها، وكذا الثالثة ساعة تزوجها مرة أخرى.

وقال أبو يوسف: لا يقع أخرى حتى يمضي شهر من الأولى. كذا في «الذخيرة».

قوله: (والسنة في الوقت: تثبت في المدخول بها خاصة، وهو أن يطلقها في طهر لم يجامعها فيه، أو حاملا قد استبان حملها. لأنه إذا طلقها في حال الحيض: طول عليها العدة، وإن طلقها في طهر قد جامعها فيه: لم يؤمن أن تكون علقت من ذلك الجماع، فيندم)
Book of Divorce. The sunnah in divorce is from two aspects: sunnah in time, and sunnah in number. As for the sunnah in number, it is the same for the consummated wife and the non-consummated. Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) would not be brought a man who divorced three times except that he inflicted painful punishment. Likewise, pronouncing two divorces in one menstrual purity is bid'ah. Likewise, divorce during menstruation is disliked because it lengthens the waiting period for the woman. Likewise during postpartum bleeding. There is a difference of narration concerning the one irrevocable divorce: It was said in al-Asl that he has erred against the sunnah because there is no need to establish an extra attribute (irrevocability) in the dissolution. In al-Ziyadat: it is not disliked due to the need for immediate dissolution. * His statement: 'The sunnah in divorce is from two aspects: sunnah in time and sunnah in number. As for the sunnah in number, it is the same for the consummated wife and the non-consummated.' The sunnah in time is established specifically for the consummated wife, which is that he divorces her one time in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her. Because triple divorce in one word is prohibited only out of fear of regret, that he might change his mind and reconsider the contract with her again, and this meaning exists for the non-consummated wife as well. And it is said: The sunnah in number is the best divorce, which is that he divorces her once, no more. And the one is called 'number' metaphorically because it is the basis of number. If she is non-consummated, then the sunnah is achieved in her divorce without paying attention to any other matter. If she is consummated, then it is necessary to consider the time: if it is suitable for pronouncing, it is sunni (following sunnah), and if not, it is bid'i (innovative). His statement: 'It is the same for the consummated and non-consummated.' Even if he says before consummation: 'You are divorced three times with the intention of sunnah,' one divorce occurs immediately when he speaks. If he marries her again, another occurs at the moment of marriage, and similarly the third when he marries her again. Abu Yusuf said: Another does not occur until a month passes from the first. As found in al-Dhakhirah. His statement: 'The sunnah in time is established specifically for the consummated wife, and that is that he divorces her in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, or if she is pregnant whose pregnancy is apparent.' Because if he divorces her during menstruation, he lengthens her waiting period, and if he divorces her in a state of purity in which he has had intercourse with her, it is not safe from the possibility that she might have conceived from that intercourse, so he might regret.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayirah, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, discusses the sunnah and bid'ah classifications of divorce (talaq). The author states that sunnah divorce has two dimensions: sunnah in number and sunnah in time. Sunnah in number means that the husband pronounces a single divorce (talaq wahidah) per instance, and this applies equally to consummated and non-consummated marriages. The best form of divorce according to the sunnah is one pronouncement only. The term 'one' is figuratively called 'number' because it is the origin of counting. For non-consummated wives, the sunnah is satisfied regardless of timing; for consummated wives, proper timing (a pure state without recent intercourse) is also required to avoid regret or extended waiting periods. The passage also explains that triple divorce in one utterance is prohibited due to the fear of regret. It then addresses the ruling of an irrevocable single divorce (al-wahidah al-ba'inah) during a non-menstrual period: according to al-Asl, it is against the sunnah because it adds irrevocability unnecessarily; according to al-Ziyadat, it is not disliked because the husband may need immediate dissolution. Finally, the commentary notes a difference of opinion on when subsequent divorces fall after marriage: the general view is they occur immediately upon marriage, while Abu Yusuf holds that one month must elapse from the first divorce. The text uses the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab (painful punishment for triple talaq) as evidence, along with rational reasoning (fear of regret).

Key Terms
السنة في الطلاق (al-sunnah fi al-talaq): The method of divorce that follows the Prophet's practice: one pronouncement in a non-menstrual period without intercourse for consummated wives.
البدعي (al-bid'i): Divorce that deviates from the sunnah, such as triple divorce in one word or divorce during menstruation.
الواحدة البائنة (al-wahidah al-ba'inah): A single divorce that makes the marriage irrevocably terminated (ba'in), requiring a new marriage contract for reunion.
المدخول بها (al-madkhul biha): A wife with whom the husband has had sexual intercourse after a valid marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) One pronouncement
C) Two pronouncements
D) Four pronouncements

Key Takeaway
The sunnah divorce is one pronouncement in a non-menstrual period without intercourse for consummated wives; any deviation is bid'ah and subject to sin.

Sunnah Divorce: Conditions in Time and Number
Defines conditions for Sunnah divorce with reasons and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a Sunnah divorce in terms of time and number, and identify which wife categories each condition applies to.

Core Idea
A Sunnah divorce is one pronouncement in a state of purity after no intercourse, or during clear pregnancy.

Divorce in Islam is not a free-for-all; the Sunnah prescribes a specific method to minimize harm and allow for reconciliation. This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira defines the ideal form of divorce (ṭalāq al-sunnah) in two dimensions: when to pronounce it (time) and how many pronouncements (number). The rules differ based on whether the wife is consummated, pregnant, or non-menstruating, and the scholars discuss exceptional cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects
Recognize that Sunnah divorce has a time condition (al-sunnah fī al-waqt) and a number condition (al-sunnah fī al-ʿadad). The passage explains both.
2
Determine the wife's status
Check if the wife is consummated (madkhūl bihā) or not. This determines whether the time condition applies.
Non-consummated wives have no ʿiddah, so timing is irrelevant.
3
Apply the time condition
For a consummated wife, the ideal time is a state of purity (ṭuhr) without intercourse since the last menstruation, or clear pregnancy. Divorcing during menstruation or after intercourse is bidʿī (innovated).
The reason (ʿilla) is to avoid prolonging ʿiddah or regret from a possible pregnancy.
4
Apply the number condition
The Sunnah is to divorce once (one ṭalāq), not three at once. A triple statement is interpreted as a promise to divorce in the Sunnah manner, resulting in only one immediate divorce.
The remaining divorces occur upon subsequent remarriages, not immediately.
5
Note intra-Hanafi disputes
Abu Yusuf and Zufar differ on certain details. Understand their positions and the relied-upon (muftā bihī) view.
Abu Yusuf requires a month gap between divorces for non-menstruating women; Zufar prohibits divorce during menstruation for non-consummated wives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
والسنة في الوقت، تثبت في حق المدخول بها خاصة، وهو : أن يطلقها واحدةً فى طهر لم يجامعها فيه .
لأن الطلاق الثلاث في كلمة إنما منع منه؛ خوفاً من الندم، أن يبدو له، فيستدرك العقد عليها ثانياً، وهذا المعنى موجود في غير المدخول بها. - ويقال: إن السنة في العدد: هو أحسن الطلاق، وهو أن يطلقها واحدة، لا غير.
- وسميت الواحدة عدداً: مجازاً ؛ لأنه أصل العدد، فإن كانت غير مدخولة، فقد وجدت السُّنَّة في طلاقها من غير التفات إلى أمر آخر. وإن كانت مدخولةً : فلا بد من النظر إلى الوقت، فإن كان يصلح للإيقاع : كان سنياً، وإن لم يصلح: كان بدعياً.
وقوله : يستوي فيها المدخولة وغيرها حتى لو قال قبل الدخول: أنت طالق ثلاثاً للسنة : يقع واحدة ساعة تكلَّم، فإن تزوجها: وقعت أخرى ساعة تزوجها، وكذا الثالثة ساعة تزوجها مرة أخرى.
وقال أبو يوسف : لا يقع أخرى حتى يَمضي شهر من الأُولى. كذا في «الذخيرة».
قوله: (والسُّنَّة في الوقت : تثبت في المدخول بها خاصة، وهو أن يطلقها في طهر لم يجامعها فيه، أو حاملاً قد استبان حملها. لأنه إذا طلقها في حال الحيض: طوَّل عليها العدة، وإن طلقها في طهر قد جامعها فيه: لم يُؤمَن أن تكون عَلِقت من ذلك الجماع، فيندم على طلاقها، وهذا لا يُتصور إلا في المدخولة.
وأما غير المدخولة : فلا تثبت فيها السنَّةُ في الوقت، حتى إنه لا يكره طلاقها وهي حائض؛ لأنها لا عدة عليها. قوله: (وغير المدخول بها : يطلقها في حالة الطهر والحيض).
وقال زفر : لا يطلقها في حالة الحيض.
* قوله : (وإذا كانت المرأةُ ممن لا تحيض من صِغَر أو كبر، وأراد أن يُطلقها للسنة: طلقها واحدةً متى شاء؛ لأن المانع من طلاق الحائض تطويل العدة، وخوفُ الحَبَل، وهذا معدوم في الآيسة، والصغيرة.
وقال زفر : لا يطلقها حتى يمضي شهر بعد ما جامعها.
فإن أراد أن يحصل لها طلاق السنة بالعدد: طلقها واحدةً متى شاء، (ثم يتركها حتى يمضي شهر ، ثم يطلقها أخرى ، ثم يتركها شهراً، ثم يطلقها أخرى).
* قوله: (ويجوز أن يطلقها ولا يفصل بين وطئها وطلاقها بزمان). يعني التي لا تحيض من صِغَرٍ أو كبر.
Book of Divorce. And the Sunnah in time is established specifically for the consummated wife: that he divorces her once in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her. Because the triple divorce in one sentence is prohibited only out of fear of regret, that he might reconsider and recover the contract with her a second time, and this meaning exists in the non-consummated one. It is said: The Sunnah in number is the best divorce, which is to divorce her once, no more. And the one (single) is called 'number' metaphorically because it is the origin of number. If she is non-consummated, then the Sunnah in her divorce is found without regard to another matter. If she is consummated, then consideration of time is necessary: if it is suitable for occurrence, it is Sunní; if not, it is Bid‘í. His saying: it is equal in this regard the consummated and non-consummated; even if he says before consummation: 'You are thrice divorced according to the Sunnah,' one divorce falls at the moment he speaks; then if he marries her, another falls at the moment he marries her; and likewise the third at the moment he marries her again. Abu Yusuf said: another does not fall until a month passes from the first. As in al-Dhakhira. His saying: (And the Sunnah in time is established specifically for the consummated wife, and it is that he divorces her in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, or a pregnant woman whose pregnancy is manifest. Because if he divorces her during menstruation, he prolongs the waiting period; and if he divorces her in a state of purity in which he has had intercourse with her, it is not safe that she might have conceived from that intercourse, and he would regret his divorce. And this is conceivable only for the consummated. As for the non-consummated, the Sunnah in time is not established for her, so that it is not disliked to divorce her while she is menstruating, because she has no waiting period. His saying: (And the non-consummated wife: he divorces her in the state of purity and menstruation.) Zufar said: he should not divorce her in the state of menstruation. His saying: (And if the woman is one who does not menstruate due to youth or old age, and he wants to divorce her according to the Sunnah: he divorces her once whenever he wishes; because the prohibition of divorcing a menstruating woman is based on prolonging the waiting period and fear of pregnancy, and this is absent in the post-menopausal and the minor. Zufar said: he should not divorce her until a month passes after he had intercourse with her. If he wants to achieve for her the Sunnah divorce in number: he divorces her once whenever he wishes, then leaves her until a month passes, then divorces her another, then leaves her a month, then divorces her another. His saying: (And it is permissible for him to divorce her without separating between intercourse and divorce by any time). Meaning the one who does not menstruate due to youth or old age.)
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage defines the Sunnah divorce (ṭalāq al-sunnah) in two aspects: time and number. For time, the Sunnah is only applicable to a consummated marriage: the husband must divorce her with one pronouncement during a pure period (ṭuhr) in which he has not had intercourse with her, or while she is clearly pregnant. The reason (ʿilla) is to avoid prolonging the ʿiddah (waiting period) or regret after a possible pregnancy. For a non-consummated wife, there is no such time restriction; divorcing her during menstruation is not disliked. In terms of number, the Sunnah is to divorce her once, not three at once. The text also addresses a triple divorce before consummation: if the husband says 'you are thrice divorced according to the Sunnah,' only one divorce occurs immediately, and subsequent divorces occur upon each remarriage. Abu Yusuf differs, holding that the second divorce does not occur until a month after the first. For women who do not menstruate (young or old), the Sunnah is to divorce her once at any time, and then wait a month between each subsequent divorce to achieve the Sunnah in number. Zufar's opinion that even for non-consummated wives, divorce during menstruation is disallowed is rejected by the majority.

Key Terms
السنة في الوقت (al-sunnah fī al-waqt): The recommended condition regarding the timing of divorce: to divorce in a state of purity not touched, or during clear pregnancy.
السنة في العدد (al-sunnah fī al-ʿadad): The recommended number of divorces: one at a time, not three simultaneously.
المدخول بها (al-madkhūl bihā): A wife with whom the husband has consummated the marriage.
طلاق بدعي (ṭalāq bidʿī): Divorce that violates the Sunnah in time (e.g., during menstruation or in a state of purity after intercourse).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a triple talaq pronounced as 'أنت طالق ثلاثاً للسنة' before consummation?
A) All three divorces occur immediately.
B) One divorce occurs immediately; the second upon remarriage; the third upon another remarriage.
C) No divorce occurs until one month passes.
D) The divorce is invalid and not counted.

Key Takeaway
The Sunnah divorce requires one pronouncement at the proper time (for consummated wives) and, if multiple divorces are intended, a month gap between each.
